<div id="reproducible-research-peer-assessment-1" class="section level1">
<h1>Reproducible Research: Peer Assessment 1</h1>
</div>
<div id="loading-and-preprocessing-the-data" class="section level1">
<h1>Loading and preprocessing the data</h1>
<p>For this analysis we will need the <code>ggplot2</code> and <code>dplyr</code> packages. The first one will be used for plotting and second to transform the data when necessary.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>library(ggplot2)
library(dplyr)</code></pre>
<p>We will load the data only if is not present in the directory.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>if (!file.exists(&quot;activity.zip&quot;)) {
    url &lt;- &quot;https://d396qusza40orc.cloudfront.net/repdata%2Fdata%2Factivity.zip&quot;
    download.file(url, destfile = &quot;activity.zip&quot;, method = &quot;curl&quot;)
    unzip(&quot;activity.zip&quot;)
}</code></pre>
<p>Once the data downloaded and unzipped, we can read the file using <code>read.csv</code> and turn the <code>date</code> column into an object of class <code>Date</code>.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activity &lt;- read.csv(&quot;activity.csv&quot;)
activity$date &lt;- as.Date(activity$date)
str(activity)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## 'data.frame':    17568 obs. of  3 variables:
##  $ steps   : int  NA NA NA NA NA NA NA NA NA NA ...
##  $ date    : Date, format: &quot;2012-10-01&quot; &quot;2012-10-01&quot; ...
##  $ interval: int  0 5 10 15 20 25 30 35 40 45 ...</code></pre>
<p>A quick summary of the data shows that we have some missing values.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>summary(activity)</code></pre>
<pre><code>##      steps            date               interval   
##  Min.   :  0.0   Min.   :2012-10-01   Min.   :   0  
##  1st Qu.:  0.0   1st Qu.:2012-10-16   1st Qu.: 589  
##  Median :  0.0   Median :2012-10-31   Median :1178  
##  Mean   : 37.4   Mean   :2012-10-31   Mean   :1178  
##  3rd Qu.: 12.0   3rd Qu.:2012-11-15   3rd Qu.:1766  
##  Max.   :806.0   Max.   :2012-11-30   Max.   :2355  
##  NA's   :2304</code></pre>
<p>For the first part of the analysis we will discard missing value.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activitynona &lt;- activity[!is.na(activity$steps), ]</code></pre>
</div>
<div id="what-is-the-mean-total-number-of-steps-taken-per-day" class="section level1">
<h1>What is the mean total number of steps taken per day?</h1>
<pre class="r"><code>activityday &lt;- activitynona %&gt;%
    group_by(date) %&gt;%
    summarise(totalsteps = sum(steps, na.rm = TRUE))</code></pre>
<p>With the histogram we can see that most of the people take approximatively 10000 per day.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>  ggplot(activityday, aes(totalsteps)) +
  geom_histogram(aes(y = ..density..),
  fill = &quot;steelblue&quot;,
  colour = &quot;white&quot;,
  binwidth = 3000) +
  labs(x = &quot;Total Steps per day&quot;) +
  theme_bw()</code></pre>

<p>There is no difference between the median number of steps per day and average number of steps. This result was predictable since the distribution of the total number of step is quite symetric (see histogram).</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activityday %&gt;%
    summarise(meansteps = mean(totalsteps),
          mediansteps = median(totalsteps))</code></pre>
<pre><code>## Source: local data frame [1 x 2]
## 
##   meansteps mediansteps
## 1     10766       10765</code></pre>
</div>
<div id="what-is-the-average-daily-activity-pattern" class="section level1">
<h1>What is the average daily activity pattern?</h1>
<p>We will now analyze the activity pattern by interval.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activity5min &lt;- activitynona %&gt;%
    group_by(interval) %&gt;%
    summarise(avgsteps = mean(steps))</code></pre>
<p>The maximum number of steps was taken at interval :</p>
<pre class="r"><code>(intervalmax &lt;- activity5min$interval[which.max(activity5min$avgsteps)])</code></pre>
<pre><code>## [1] 835</code></pre>
<p>And the maximum number of steps is</p>
<pre class="r"><code>(stepmax &lt;- max(activity5min$avgsteps))</code></pre>
<pre><code>## [1] 206.2</code></pre>
<p>The graph below shows the activity pattern by interval with a peak around the interval 835</p>
<pre class="r"><code>  ggplot(activity5min, aes(interval, avgsteps)) +
      geom_line(colour = &quot;steelblue&quot;) +
      geom_point(x = intervalmax,
                 y = stepmax,
                 colour = &quot;red&quot;, 
                 shape = 19, size = 0.8) +
      geom_segment(x = intervalmax, y = 0,
                   xend = intervalmax,
                   yend = stepmax,
                   linetype = &quot;dashed&quot;, colour = &quot;red&quot;,
                   size = 0.07, alpha = 0.1) +
     scale_x_continuous(breaks = c(0, 500, 
                intervalmax, 1000, 1500, 2000)) +
  labs(x = &quot;Interval&quot;, y = &quot;Average steps&quot;) +
  theme_bw()</code></pre>

<div id="imputing-missing-values" class="section level1">
<h1>Imputing missing values</h1>
<p>We have a lot of missing rows in the datasets</p>
<pre class="r"><code>sum(!complete.cases(activity))</code></pre>
<pre><code>## [1] 2304</code></pre>
<p>All the missing data are in fact in the <code>steps</code> variable</p>
<pre class="r"><code>sum(is.na(activity$steps))</code></pre>
<pre><code>## [1] 2304</code></pre>
<p>To replace the missing values in the <code>steps</code> variable we will replace each missing data by the median data for corresponding the day of the week (Monday, Tuesday, etc.) at the interval considered. For example if the data is missing a monday at the interval 900 we will use the median value (discarding missing value) of all monday at the interval 900. In this exercice the median is prefered to the average because it is more robust to outlier.</p>
<p>We will first create an index of weekday-interval and split the data in two parts : missing and non missing data</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activity$wdmin &lt;- weekdays(activity$date)
activity$wdmin &lt;- paste0(activity$wdmin, activity$interval)
activitynona &lt;- activity[!is.na(activity$steps), ]
activityna &lt;- activity[is.na(activity$steps), ]</code></pre>
<p>The next step is to compute the median per weekday-interval</p>
<pre class="r"><code>toimpute &lt;- activity %&gt;%
    group_by(wdmin) %&gt;%
    summarise(steps = median(steps, na.rm = TRUE))
sample_n(toimpute, 5)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## Source: local data frame [5 x 2]
## 
##              wdmin steps
## 751   Saturday2245     0
## 1155   Thursday100     0
## 1830 Wednesday1710    61
## 406     Monday1830    60
## 1808 Wednesday1525     0</code></pre>
<p>Now we have the data to impute we can merge it to the original data</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activityna$steps &lt;- NULL
activityna &lt;- inner_join(activityna, toimpute)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## Joining by: &quot;wdmin&quot;</code></pre>
<pre class="r"><code>activityfilled &lt;- rbind(activityna, activitynona)
activityfilled &lt;- activityfilled %&gt;% arrange(date, interval)</code></pre>
<p>With the filled data it is possible to have to total number of steps per day without discarding any data</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activitydayfilled &lt;- activityfilled %&gt;%
group_by(date) %&gt;%
summarise(totalsteps = sum(steps))</code></pre>
<p>Let’s compute the mean and median steps with the filled data</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activitydayfilled %&gt;%
summarise(meansteps = mean(totalsteps),
mediansteps = median(totalsteps))</code></pre>
<pre><code>## Source: local data frame [1 x 2]
## 
##   meansteps mediansteps
## 1      9705       10395</code></pre>
<p>The difference between median and mean is more pronounced with the filled data compared to the original data with missing values.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>ggplot(activitydayfilled, aes(totalsteps)) +
    geom_histogram(aes(y = ..density..),
           fill = &quot;steelblue&quot;,
           colour = &quot;white&quot;,
           binwidth = 3000) +
  labs(x = &quot;Total steps&quot;) +
  theme_bw()</code></pre>

title="plot of chunk unnamed-chunk-21" alt="plot of chunk unnamed-chunk-21" width="672" /></p>
<p>The histogram shows a difference at the tail of the distribution and the density plot below highlight this difference between the original data and filled one. In fact, the graph in blue (the filled data) shows a heavier tail than the graph in red (original data). This difference doesn’t affect the median but the mean which is more sensitive to distributions tails differ signifcantly.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>ggplot(activitydayfilled, aes(totalsteps)) +
    geom_density(fill = &quot;steelblue&quot;,
    colour = &quot;white&quot;,
    binwidth = 3000,
    alpha = 0.2) +
    geom_density(aes(x = totalsteps),
    fill = &quot;red&quot;,
    colour = &quot;white&quot;,
    binwidth = 3000,
    alpha = 0.2,
    data = activityday) +
    labs(x = &quot;Total steps&quot;) +
    geom_text(x = 275, y = 0.00005,
              label = &quot;filled&quot;,
              colour = &quot;steelblue&quot;) +
    geom_text(x = 17000, y = 0.00005,
              label = &quot;original&quot;,
              colour = &quot;red&quot;) +
    theme_bw()</code></pre>

<div id="are-there-differences-in-activity-patterns-between-weekdays-and-weekends" class="section level1">
<h1>Are there differences in activity patterns between weekdays and weekends?</h1>
<p>Let’s create a function to separate the date in weekend and weekday.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>weekend &lt;- function(date) {
    ifelse(is.element(weekdays(date), c(&quot;Saturday&quot;,  &quot;Sunday&quot;)),
       &quot;weekend&quot;, &quot;weekday&quot;)
}</code></pre>
<p>Now we can apply this function to the filled data</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activityfilled$weekday &lt;- weekend(activityfilled$date)
table(activityfilled$weekday)</code></pre>
<pre><code>## 
## weekday weekend 
##   12960    4608</code></pre>
<p>With this new variable we can check if there is a difference of activity if we are in week-end or not.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>activitywkd &lt;- activityfilled %&gt;%
    group_by(weekday, interval) %&gt;%
    summarise(wkavgsteps = mean(steps))</code></pre>
<p>The graph below highlight a different behavior between activity done in weekday and weekend. There is slightly more activity in the week end and in particular around interval 1000 and 1500.</p>
<pre class="r"><code>ggplot(activitywkd, aes(interval, wkavgsteps)) +
geom_line(colour = &quot;steelblue&quot;) +
facet_wrap( ~ weekday, ncol = 1) +
labs(x = &quot;Interval&quot;, y = &quot;Average steps&quot;) +
theme_bw()</code></pre>
